## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (classical mechanics) ŌĆö nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration given position x, velocity v, and time t, which is the standard state-space form for second-order oscillators (x_dot=v, v_dot=f(x,v,t)). Nonlinear harmonic oscillators commonly include nonlinear restoring forces, nonlinear damping, and optional periodic/parametric forcing in time.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator (undamped): dv_dt = -(c0**2) * x (restoring force proportional to displacement)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = -(c0**2) * x - c1 * v (viscous damping)
- Shifted equilibrium spring: dv_dt = -(c0**2) * (x - c1) - c2 * v (oscillation about offset equilibrium)
- Coulomb (dry) friction + spring: dv_dt = -(c0**2) * x - c1 * v - c2 * (v / (Abs(v) + c3)) (smooth approximation to -c2*sign(v))
- Quadratic/drag-like damping: dv_dt = -(c0**2) * x - c1 * v - c2 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-like nonlinear dissipation)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -(c0**2) * x - c1 * v - c2 * x**3 (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- General odd restoring force (polynomial): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 - c3 * v (higher-order conservative stiffness + viscous loss)
- Nonlinear stiffness with rational softening: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x / (c2 + x**2) - c3 * v (stiffness decreases with amplitude)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (state-dependent damping producing limit cycles)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent damping): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - v**2) * v (self-excited oscillations via nonlinear damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = -(c0**2) * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t + c4) (periodic external forcing)
- Parametrically excited oscillator (Mathieu-type): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness / parametric resonance)
- Li├®nard form (broad nonlinear oscillator family): dv_dt = -f(x) * v - g(x) with f(x)=c0 + c1 * x**2, g(x)=c2 * x + c3 * x**3 (captures many nonlinear oscillators including Duffing/van der Pol variants)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring dynamics ŌåÆ dv_dt depends primarily on x (often as an odd function: -x, -x^3, -x^5), reflecting symmetry about x=0.
- Dissipation ŌåÆ terms odd in v (e.g., -c*v, -c*v*Abs(v), -c*v/(Abs(v)+c)) remove energy and yield decay to equilibrium.
- Self-excitation / limit cycles ŌåÆ state-dependent damping like (c0 - x**2)*v or (c0 - v**2)*v injects energy at small amplitude and dissipates at large amplitude.
- External periodic driving ŌåÆ explicit sinusoidal dependence on t (cos(c*t+c)) produces forced oscillations, resonance peaks, and phase locking.
- Parametric resonance ŌåÆ time-periodic modulation multiplying x (e.g., -(c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x) indicates stiffness modulation and instability tongues.
- Hardening vs softening stiffness ŌåÆ positive cubic term in restoring force (-(... + c*x^3)) shifts frequency upward with amplitude; negative shifts it downward.
- Dry friction signatures ŌåÆ nearly constant-magnitude opposing-velocity term (Ōēł-c*sign(v)), often modeled smoothly via v/(Abs(v)+c).
- Amplitude-dependent frequency/damping ŌåÆ rational or polynomial functions of x or v (e.g., x/(c+x**2), x^5, v*Abs(v)) encode nonlinearity that grows with amplitude.

GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - beta*sin(x)*v - c1*beta*v
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.0313132*v┬│ - 0.657729*v*sin(x) - 1.31546*v + 0.383671*sin(t)`

The key basis functions in GT are:
1. `sin(t)` ŌĆö sinusoidal in t
2. `v` ŌĆö linear in v
3. `v┬│` ŌĆö cubic in v
4. `v*sin(x)` ŌĆö product of v and sin(x)

The critical term is `v*sin(x)`. This is a product of v with a trigonometric function of x. Let me check what structural forms the candidates offer for the x-dependent term.

Most candidates have terms like `v/sqrt(c+x)`, `v/x┬▓`, `v*x`, `v*(c+x)^c`, `v*x^c`, or `v/x^(1/5)`. None of these are `v*sin(x)`.

**Key question:** Can any of these x-dependent terms equal `v*sin(x)`?

- `v/sqrt(c+x)` ŌĆö this is algebraic in x, not trigonometric. Cannot equal `v*sin(x)`.
- `v/x┬▓` ŌĆö algebraic, not trigonometric.
- `v*x` ŌĆö polynomial, not trigonometric.
- `v*(c+x)^c` ŌĆö power function, not trigonometric.
- `v*x^c` ŌĆö power function, not trigonometric.
- `v/x^(1/5)` ŌĆö power function, not trigonometric.
- `v/(c+x)┬▓` ŌĆö algebraic, not trigonometric.

By the principle of linear independence of basis functions (Rule 3), algebraic/power functions of x cannot equal `sin(x)` for all x in the domain. Since `sin(x)` is a transcendental trigonometric function and none of the candidates contain `sin(x)` multiplied by `v`, **none of the candidates can match the GT**.

Let me also check candidates with `exp(c*x)` terms (Candidates 19, 33, 34): exponential functions are also linearly independent from `sin(x)`, so these cannot match either.

Candidate 32, 36-39, 44, 46, 48, 50 have `v*(c+x)^c` type terms ŌĆö power functions cannot equal `sin(x)`.

Candidate 35, 45 have `x*(c+v)^5` terms ŌĆö these mix x and v in a non-separable way different from `v*sin(x)`.

Candidate 44 has `t*(c+x)^c` ŌĆö introduces t-dependence in a non-sinusoidal way.

Let me verify systematically that NO candidate contains a `sin(x)` term or any trigonometric function of x:

Looking through all 50 candidates: Every candidate has `sin(c + c*t)` (sinusoidal in t), but NONE have `sin(x)` or any trigonometric function of x. The x-dependent terms are all algebraic/power functions.

Since `v*sin(x)` is an essential basis function in the GT that cannot be represented by any algebraic or power function of x, none of the candidates can match.
